<Author>aspine67
<Content>Great value The hotel is in a great location - 10 minutes from the Eiffel Tower, 1 minute from restaurants, bakeries and supermarkets in the Rue Cler area, and about 3 minutes from the Ecole Militaire metro station. There's even a direct bus to the Champs Elysees outside the hotel, although we never used it (took the metro). It's a very safe area and we didn't have any problems walking back from the Eiffel Tower at 10pm at night. The free Internet access in the lobby is brilliant.Must do: You must go up the Eiffel Tower at night - 9pm is a good time as the queues are shorter. The lights on the Eiffel Tower flash for 10 minutes on the hour at nights and it's the most beautiful sight.Must try: crepes at Cafe Ulysse en Gaul, breakfast at Cafe du Marche (both at Rue Cler), across from the hotel - Fontaine de Jade for good Chinese food and Le Bosquet for excellent French onion soup, and Punjab restaurant (1 minute past the Ecole Militaire station) for great Indian food and some of the best restaurant service in Paris.

<Author>lhinesabc
<Content>An "ok" stay I just returned from my second stay at this hotel, this time with my older parents in a second room. While I have read the enthusiastic reviews of the hotel on this website, I have to say they may be creating an impression that may not meet expectations. The rooms are indeed on the large side for Paris and are prettily decorated and somewhat cozy. The bathrooms are very standard, but do have nice towels. The neighborhood near the metro and the Rue Cler is great and the two computers in the lobby are a wonderful convenience. I did not find the staff,except for Frederique, to be very friendly, though they were efficient. The hotel itself is beginning to need renovation, with peeling paint, stained wallpaper and badly stained carpeting in both of our rooms. The noise factor is a problem. The walls are paper thin and the noise from the elevator and staff banging around starts at 6:30am. We are not light sleepers, but it was tough. I will probably investigate other hotels before staying here again.

<Author>jpi
<Content>Weekend in Paris at Hotel Relais-Bosquet We stayed at the 3 star Hotel Relais-Bosquet in the RueCler district and it was 2 blocks from Eiffel Tower park. Everything was right outside our hotel and the metro 1 block away. This is the second time we have stayed in this district but this location and hotel was very good. Recommended by Rick Steves, we got free breakfast which was good. Also, booked an online special so it was only 130 euros/night with free breakfast and 2 tickets to the Louve. The desk personel were very helpful with all our needs. Extras:Two free computers available in the lobby; clean and neat even tho the building was on the older side; updated room with big bed and wonderful fresh feeling sheets; flat screen TV (in case you need CNN); two wastebaskets in room; refrigerator in room with coffee/tea making service; updated bathroom with separate room for toilet; big, fluffy towels. Restaurants in the area are abundant from small cafes to full scale. The bakeri around the corner is wonderful and a grocery store that sells good inexpensive wine just by the metro. I would stay at the HOtel Relias-Bosquet again and recommend it for a true Parisian experience in a wonderful neighborhood.

<Author>ColWarne
<Content>Best value in Paris! I've used quite a few Paris hotels and this was certainly an excellent choice. A very comfortable hotel in a very nice district of Paris, with easy travel to all the attractions. Staff extremely helpful - for example, when we were wrongly told that breakfast was served until 12 on the Sunday and we appeared at 11.15 to find the room being vacuumed, we were immediately offered what turned out to be an excellent (and cheaper!) breakfast in the room. The costs of the room compared well with Paris hotels generally, especially the reduced rate for 3 days. Tea and coffee facilities are provided, which is often not the case in Paris. Decent size bath towels too! Minor quibbles were the fact that free internet was provided, but that the signal was very weak in the room we had. However, there are two free computers to use in the very comfortable reception area. And there was some minor sound disturbance from water draining from another room and people using the stairs, but we were so tired it didn't matter. I鈥檝e already booked to stay there again, on business, so that's got to be the best recommendation. PS: The restaurant recommended by reception - Le Bosquet, over the road - was excellent and very reasonably priced. It鈥檚 also worth travelling into the Marais to eat at L'Epouvanteil (6 rue de Jarente). Lovely food from a three course menu @ 28鈧?and a brilliant host, who really wanted a group of 10 of us to enjoy our time there.

<Content>Adequate The hotel is located near Rue Clur street and convenient to a train station. The area is cute, although there were homeless on the street. Not that the staff did anything wrong, but when you are on vacation you value that little extra attention, even if it is a smile or asking how your day was going. Based on the other reviews here I guess I had higher expectations.Paris in general was great. Our experience was that people were generally helpful and nice. We felt like welcome guests in the city.

<Author>RBL52
<Content>Perfect Parisian Experience We just stayed at Hotel Relais Bosquet for a week ending on November 20, 2008. We had done extensive research about the hotel and were thrilled to find the positive comments we had read were justified. The staff at Relais Bosquet could not have been more accommodating and helpful with information, especially bus and metro directions and restaurant recommendations and reservations. Their genuineness and willingness to help made our stay so comfortable. Our room was on the top floor (#64) and the view out the window at night of the twinkling Eiffel Tower was magnificent. The electric blinds and quiet neighborhood made sleeping very conducive, which was quite helpful. We felt it was a bargain, especially for the size of the room and bathroom facilities, at 205E a night. The Rue Cler neighborhood in which Relais Bosquet is located was perfect. It is walkable to many places (stores, outdoor markets, bistros, boulangeries, patisseries) and also situated near 3 metro stops and 2 bus lines, all which helped us to see as much of Paris as we could in the most efficient manner. It is a perfect location to see the traditional tourist sights of Paris, while providing a quiet nieghborhood at the end of the day to return to and have a glass of wine while watching Parisians on their way home from work stopping at Rue Cler's many outdoor markets. The best part of the hotel's neighborhood is the abundance of truly excellent well-priced restaurants offering various styles of cuisine, from modern trendy French, Basque, traditional French, bistro food - all priced very competitively. It is our pleasure to highly recommend Hotel Relais Bosquet, its personnel (Christian, in particular), its location and its ambience to all age groups. (Even though there were no children at the hotel when we were there, it would be a perfect location to stay with children, as the surrounding Rue Cler market area and park near the Eiffel Tower would provide great areas for children to run and play.)

<Author>davidleeds
<Content>Location makes this hotel a great place to stay I agree with most of what has been said about the hotel. I'm a Rick Steves fan and his tips make all the difference in our trips. The location is perfect for walking or buses or the metro. The restaurants in the area make a stay in Paris affordable as did the food shops. We liked Tribeca the best and it is really great value with a main course including tip and tax from 9 - 11 euros . It is a pity that all the outdoor eating is really off limits if you aren't a smoker. The hotel itself is somewhat tired in the public areas and there are plans to redo it sometime in the future. I was initially put off by the amount of dust on the carpet in the halls and am surprised it hasn't been noted in any review. We had a superior room in the courtyard which we requested.and it was very clean. It was a good size with lots of storage, two large windows in the bedroom and one in the bathroom and very quiet in terms of noise from the outside. While smoking is permitted there was no hint of smoke.The windows were always left open by the cleaning staff and the room felt fresh and airy. The bathroom had a big tub and shower which was great and double sinks with lots of counter space and there was always hot water. It is also great if you have to rinse out clothes and hang them up since there are racks that work really well. The one drawback was the toilet which was in a separate room but it was across the room from the bathroom and felt very closed in. It was beside the bed and the sound of flushing from other rooms could be heard. The breakfast was ample and the staff serving it excellent. Christian and the other men at the front desk were all pleasant and very helpful. While I have noted some issues with the hotel I would still recommend it highly. The tea/coffee bar in the room was a plus and having real china and cutlery a nice touch. We felt comfortable, safe and happy with our choice of hotel and neighbourhood

<Author>Mazowin
<Content>Loved the Relais Bosquet We spent 4 nights at the Hotel Relais Bosquet in early October. The hotel is extremely comfortable and cheerful, rooms are ample in size for two people, and the closet space is exceptional. I loved the bathroom with an actual shower door (important for Americans who are used to shower curtains/doors). One morning the light in the toilet room was burned out---we meant to tell the front desk but forgot. Nevertheless, the light was replaced by the time we returned to our room in the afternoon. Good attention to details here.We faced the street with two large windows, but we never heard any street noise unless we wanted to. Location cannot be beat---access to the Metro, Rue Cler, and city buses is very easy. The hotel is within walking distance of major sights, and there are many restaurants and cafes nearby. Frederique at the front desk was extremely helpful with making dinner reservations and calling cabs, and she did it all with a smile!

<Author>RogueFour
<Content>Very happy! We stayed at Relais Bosquet for three nights in early September. We were very pleased. First, the location was terrific ... close to the Eiffel Tower, restaurants and the metro. There was also a great little bistro across the street that we visited often.We arrived early, and even though breakfast was technically over, they allowed us to eat and served us coffee as we waited for our room to be readied. They let us store our luggage as well.We stayed the first two nights in a standard room. Wow, a view of the Eiffel Tower! Sure, it was a small room, but I have stayed in smaller in Europe, so it wasn't a problem. We knew in advance we would have to switch rooms to a superior for the third night (we booked late and that was the only way they could accommodate). We packed our stuff, but just had to leave it in the room and the attendants moved it for us!The superior room, well, what can I say? Wish we would have booked it for all three nights if we could have. Very roomy for Europe, and of course, we also once again got the Eiffel view!Great base for Paris, clean, with free wireless in the room. You should feel very comfortable reserving this boutique hotel.

<Author>daisymaescragg
<Content>Relais Bosquet is in the center of the real Paris! I read reviews for months before choosing Relais Bosquet for our 30th anniversary and this lovely little gem did not disappoint us. Getting room #64 is worth the price of a superior room rate (195 Euro, or $300.) You truly can watch a 2/3 view of the Eiffel Tower twinkling from the bed! Of course the free use of internet in the lobby is great, but the favorite amenity for this High Ball drinking southern gal is the Ice Machine!! There is a coffee maker in the room, a refrigerator, and great A/C. The fantastic Metro is a block away, and with no longer than 5 minutes between trains, you can get anywhere in minutes. Be sure to buy 10 tickets at a time (a carnet) and you won't hav to waste a minute in this beautiful city! (aThe electric shades are loved by all, and you are right in the middle of the bustling rue Clare neighborhood. I really get weary oftravelers complaining about street noise--I would never travel without little foam earplugs. Brush up on your French,-this is truly a place the locals love, and not all the cartes (Menu) are in English, although most wait staff understand English, it is appreciated if you at least attempt a few words.

<Author>BeHappyM8
<Content>Nicest Hotel in Rue Cler area We stayed here because from our Trip Advisor Research it appeared to be the nicest of the Hotels in the Rue Cler area. And it was!From the moment Frederica welcomed us by name to the time our pick up van took us to the airport, Frederica was a welcome font of knowledge and information and maps and suggestions. And what she couldn鈥檛 help us with, the two free internet computers in the hotel鈥檚 pretty lobby solved for us.Our room a double superior room, was exactly what we were hoping for in Paris, elegantly furnished with a view of the Eiffel Tower that we marvelled at day and night. The room was ample with a big, comfortable bed, two large windows for light, a big TV, desk and room safe. The windows had electric shutters to block out the light and the noise so we slept soundly after our days of wandering the beautiful streets of Paris. The bathroom was a good size with a strong hot shower and a separate toilet in another room, almost unheard of in Europe. There was also a walk in wardrobe with an automatic light that activated as you walked past it which was particularly useful for those that need to visit the toilet in the middle of the night.Breakfast was not included but there was a bakery on the corner to the left and Rue Cler with multiple cafes and another bakery to the right. Rue Cler is just the most beautiful market street, especially on a Sunday, and definitely worth a visit. The close proximity of Relais Bosquet to the Eiffel Tower, a really good landmark to get you back home, The Ecole Militaire, the Invalides, the hop on 鈥?hop off bus, the Metro and heaps of cafes and brasseries make this an excellent yet not too touristy location.

<Author>daisybelle65
<Content>Wonderful Hotel Booked this hotel based on Rick Steves Paris Tour Book. Very well located in the Rue Cler area. Very quiet location. We had a superior room on the 3rd floor with a view of the Eiffel Tower - lovely. When we checked in we mentioned Rick Steves Book and were given complimentary breakfast - saved money and was delicious. Room service of the complimentary breakfast was also included. The room and bathroom were a nice size for Europe and clean with very adequate air conditioning. It is not terribly hot in Paris but can be very muggy and humid so the air conditioning is welcome. Plus you can keep the window closed avoiding listening to the street noise. We spent 8 days there and were very comfortable. The rooms have an electric room darkening shade that is great. The only problem was that sometimes with jet lag we woke late because of the darkness. The staff was always helpful and internet access was free and very accessible in the lobby. The area has many restaurants to choose from and is within easy walking of the metro. It was also conveniently located to the #69 bus which traverses the city and all the major historical sites. We knew of this bus from reading Rick Steves book. The Eiffel Tower was about a 10-15 minute walk from the hotel and since it stays light out until 10:30 PM a late picnic at the tower was very nice after a long day sightseeing. Would definitely stay at this hotel again and thank Rick Steves for the recommendation.

Our room and bathroom were both very clean. The hotel provided nice bathroom amenities and there was a regular hair dryer which was great. My only very small criticism is that the housekeeping staff was not very good about replacing things, but as soon as we told the front desk it was taken care of.The breakfast buffet was wonderful and included in the special rate we got. If it had not been included it would have been 15 euros per person, pretty expensive. The buffet had juice, cereal, fresh fruit, ham and cheese, wonderful rolls, croissants and pastries and a couple of hot items. The coffee each morning was excellent . The fellow who ran the breakfast room was terrific.There is free internet access which was very nice.Everyone at the front desk was very friendly, helpful and accommodating. In particular, Frederique and Christian were outstanding. They always went the extra mile for us. For example, when Frederique checked a website for us she wasn't sure if the information was up to date so she called them and got the correct (and completely different) information. The Relais Bosquet is located right near Rue Cler which is a real neighborhood street, with lots of places to eat, and every kind of store (fruit, cheese, bakery, etc.). It's a great location, convenient to the Metro and within easy walking distance of the Eiffel Tower, Les Invalides and other sites.I would love to stay there again and would highly recommend it.

<Author>DBooger
<Content>Great, despite a touch tired I'll echo the previous comments: outstanding daytime desk staff, fantastic location, clean rooms, surprisingly quiet given its great location. The hotel is 2 blocks west of the Rue Cler market, and several blocks north of the Ecole Militiare metro stop.I learned about the Rue Cler market AFTER arrival: it is basically a 2 - 3 block (mostly) pedestrian mall with prepared food, groceries, bakeries, wine shops, flowers, etc. This area seems to get a LOT of English-speaking tourist traffic, which made me happy. I tried my pidgeon French, and most vendors happily switched to English. We picniced in our room once for lunch, once for dinner.Don't be put off by the lobby or the rooms, which could use a little cosmetic freshening.The daytime desk staff is wonderful, warm and helpful. The night desk staff is adequate, but polite. If you need special assistance, get it done between 9 a.m. and 5 p.m.

<Content>Lovely Hotel - Nice Location We stayed in the Hotel Relais Bosquet our last night in France, and by the time we got there, we were very tired. After we returned home, I was charged a fee for not showing up on the day they thought we had made our reservation for...one phone call cleared the situation up with their apologies.I would definitely recommend this hotel to anyone traveling to Paris.

<Content>Absolutely wonderful in every respect. Loved the Relais Bosquet. This clean, charming, small hotel is located right in the heart of the 7th arrondisemont and adjacent to the Rue Cler market. <Author>rji1962
<Content>Perfect location We stayed here for 3 nights last week. This is the perfect little hotel to stay in central Paris. It belies its rating as a 3 star. Free internet, flat screen tv with english news channels and Villeroy and Boch crockery in the rooms are not to be found in comparable hotels elsewhere. The rooms, whilst small, are impecably clean (more so than many 5 star hotels we have been to in other parts of the world). Its location next to the Rue Cler, metro and walking distance of the Eiffel Tower, Invalides and Rodin Musuem make it very well placed. The italian restaurant along the Rue do Champ d De Mer is very good, esp if you are a veggie.The most important thing however, is the front desk team's care. Unfortunately another guest somehow checked out with one of our bags but the front desk team were hugely embarrased. Accordingly, not only did they compensate us for this (without us asking or expecting) but they traced the bag and send it on to us in the UK, no doubt at quite a cost to them. Personally, I think that is exceptional service.

<Author>Sandra909
<Content>Live like a Parisian! We stayed here for 4 days in May 2008 for our first trip to Paris. At first glance the hotel felt small and maybe a tad worn around the edges, but within a few days the nice location and great staff had won me over completely and I would gladly stay here again. The hotel was quiet, comfortable, and clean. Our room looked over the small courtyard and we never heard any traffic or noise. The small frig in the room was great for storing our purchases from the Rue Cler market street (that is just as cute as the pictures show) and from the fresh bread bakery next door. It was nice to stay in a small hotel with local flavor that didn't feel like a chain hotel. The neighborhood is safe and clean. Metro is located 1 block away and Rue Cler is on the corner. The Eiffel tower is also a short walk away. Free internet terminals in the lobby.The staff was also very helpful. They helped us locate a lost piece of luggage, gave us maps and directions, recommended restaurants, and were able to book a last minute shuttle to the airport.The hotel was great to come home to after a long day of sightseeing. In fact, we spent one rainy day just hanging out in the neighborhood because it was too perfect to leave. You will quickly get into the habit of going to the bakery for bread in the morning, buying fresh fruit on Rue Cler, and greeting the locals as you head back to your hotel or sit at one of the many cafe's in the neighborhood.Some people may find the neighborhood too quiet, or may expect more amenities from a hotel, but for us it turned out to be just right and far away from the tourist crowds, which is just what we wanted.

<Author>KristaInLondon
<Content>A Nice Touist-Class Hotel Stayed here based on reviews on the site. My goal was to stay at a nice place at less than 200 euros a night. My single was 155 euros, I think my aunt and uncle paid 185 euros for their double. Location: I loved Rue Cler. Come out of the hotel and go right. There's a grocery store right there. Then, at the corner--cafe on each side--there's a great pedestrian foodie street. Bakeries, fruit stalls, really great looking Italian butcher, and more. Some great photo opps and just a peaceful place to hang given the lack of traffic.I did not use the Metro this time, so I can't comment on proximity to Metro stations. It's about a 10-15 minute walk to the Eiffel Tower. And 10 to 15 mins to the Seine.Rooms: They are neat and tidy. Nothing fantastic. They have Air Conditioning. Also, if you bring your laptop, they'll give you a code for free wireless. There are also two PCs in the lobby, which I thought was a nice touch. One thing I liked about the rooms is that they'd given some thought as to how to prevent wear and tear on the walls...for example, on the floor behind the nightstands, there were wooden blocks to prevent the furniture from hitting the wall and leaving marks all the time.Breakfast was not included in my rate and was 15 euros. As per previous, there are lots of cafes in the area, so you can do cheaper somewhere else. (But as my uncle pointed out, you have to wait for someone to serve you somewhere else. The buffet might be nice if you're in a hurry.)All in all, I couldn't fault the Relais Bosquet. It's a nice place. If you're looking for something trendy or really modern and brand new, this isn't the place for you. (Try the Duret, which I've stayed in previously and although it's not super-central, I like the modern feel of the rooms.) But if you're looking for some place clean and tidy and friendly, the Relais Bosquet is a very solid choice.

<Author>Busmantoo
<Content>It's not in the top ten for nothing! Maybe there's no such thing as the perfect hotel in Paris, due to price, demand and so on - but this little gem gets pretty close. If you're wanting value for money then this is the one for you. It doesn't have all the amenities of the big boys but it doesn't charge top dollar either. Go on their website and book at special rates 72 hours before your stay. The breakfast is acceptable, the rooms VERY clean and comfortable but not large. Located 10 minutes from the Eiffel Tower (we found it sparkling at us through the window when we arrived late at night!) there are several good restaurants nearby and it's close to one of the city tour bus routes. <Author>Happyhubby&Daddy
<Content>Pretty good if you are a heavy sleeper As my favorite hotel was fully booked, I tried the Relais Bosquet as it was located to where I needed to be albeit a bit more expensive. The rooms are small but adequate. Skip the 15 euro breakfast and walk out of the hotel, turn left, walk 15 steps and you are at a wonderful bakery! Walk to Rue Cler for coffee at any number of cafe's.The rooms are very clean, and the bathrooms are updated. The free Wi-Fi works great..I never turned on the tv. The shutters do a great job of keeping out the light. My work in Paris kept me out until usually midnight, so I wanted to sleep in until at least 9 a.m. This is where the hotel loses points. The doors are very heavy and start slamming at around 7:00 a.m. They are very loud and woke me up each morning.My other complaint is that the night desk people are uninpsired to help customers. They are there because they have to be. Not even a good evening when I came in at night. On the other hand, Christian and Frederica were very helpful.I would suggest another hotel if you want to sleep past 7:00. If you want to get up early, and hit the sites, the hotel is adequate.

<Author>Tomtravel23
<Content>Enjoyed the Relais Bosquet We booked the Relais Bosquet based on the tripadvisor recommendations and it met our expectations. The hotel is very low key. The staff was professional, could converse in English, and was pleased to help. Having two computers in the lobby for checking email was a real plus (but getting comfortable with the French keyboard took some time). The electric shutters on the windows were very effective in shutting out the light and outside noise. While our bed was comfortable and the bathroom large by European standards, the room itself was nothing to write home about. The neighborhood is very nice, but predominately residential, so don't expect a nightlife hotbed. You are two minutes away from a Metro stop (with a classy Lenotre shop close by) and only ten minutes from the Eiffel Tower. Strolling the nearby Rue Cler was a nice plus for our stay.

<Author>downstream23
<Content>Lived Up To Reviews I travel often to Paris on business, and like to try different hotels. Normally I stay in either the L'Opera area (our company headquarters in located in the 9th), or the Left Bank, and take the metro. I read all of the favorable comments on the Hotel Relais Bosquet, and decided to give it a try. I stayed for 4 nights and couldn't be more pleased. The room was larger than most other boutique hotels, with a large plasma screen tv and a much larger bathroom than I was accustomed to. The staff was friendly, the breakfast was much better than most (included scrambled eggs as well as the normal French breakfast), and the location near rue Cler and the Eiffel Tower was great. Also, the Ecole Militaire metro (#8 line) is just 2 blocks away, and a 10-minute ride to L'Opera, or a 2-minute ride to the connection to the Latin Quarter on the 10 line - very convenient.If there's any downside, it is that the hotel is not in the middle of all the activity and restaurants of the Latin Quarter/St. Germaine area, where I also stay. However, for many this would be an advantage.Great place!

<Author>HeikeM
<Content>Nice little hotel, great location We spent 3 days in Paris in February. It was our first stay in Paris and we were a bit anxious to find an OK hotel because we had heard that there are a lot of overpriced hotels in Paris. But he Relais Bosquet was really good. We arrived at Orly and took a taxi to the hotel. Since it was 8pm there wasn't too much traffic and we arrived after 25min. The taxi only cost 25 Euros (plus 2 Euros for each suitcase). The people at the reception were quite efficient and we immediately got our key. The room was a bit on the small side, but tasetfully decorated. The bathroom was very clean and toiletries like shower gel. shampoo, body lotion etc. were provided. The best thing was that we could see the Eiffel tower from our window even though we didn't book a superior room!When we asked for a restaurant, the people at the reception recommended The Bosquet which is just opposite the hotel. The waiters all speak Englishand I got the impression that there are a lot of English-speaking tourists at the hotel and the restaurant. There is also a very nice restaurant at Ave Bosquet - Nabuchodonosor, which serves fantastic French food.The location was excellent - just 10min away from the Eiffel tour. If you like long walks then it's possible to walk to all the main attractions. We would definitely stay again at the Relais Bosquet.

<Author>Gasheads
<Content>Great value, superb location My wife and I booked a 3 night stay after reading the great reviews on Trip Advisor and we certainly were not disappointed with our first visit to Paris. We travelled by Metro to and from CDG Airport which is relatively straightforward and much cheaper than by taxi or shuttle. If your thinking of using the Metro then take RER B to Saint-Michel Notre Dame, switching to RER C. Take RER C to Invalides where you can then hop onto the Metro line 8 to Ecole Militaire. However the metro only runs from 5.45 so no good for early flights.The location is just perfect and the main attractions are easily accessable, and if you don't fancy long, brisk walks then Metro is just yards away.We paid an extra 鈧?0 for a supreme room and it was spacious, well equipped, warm and very clean. Contrary to some opinion we also thought the bed was comfortable. The staff are very friendly, speak good English and are always on hand if needed.We didn't eat breakfast in the hotel due to the massively inflated price and there are plenty of cheaper places to eat if you look. We just loved the little patisserie a few doors down. The local restraunts didn't blow us away with their quality but were reasonably good value and staff were polite, however vegetarians be aware as you may be restricted to salad.Overall, I can't recommend this hotel enough especially if it's your first visit to Paris. It's in a lovely part of Paris and we always felt safe and welcome. We would definately consider it in future.

<Author>graycee_nf
<Content>Birthday to Remember My husband took me to Paris for my Birthday and we stayed at the charming Hotel Relais Bosquet. Frederica, front desk staff at the hotel was very helpful with suggesting 2 wonderful restaurants. We wanted to stay within the neighborhood and she recommended, L'Affriole and Floramond. Each very good and the service good at LAffriole, but superior at Floramond. We enjoyed our dinner with residents from the local neighborhoods.The rooms at the hotel were large compared to European standards and we stayed in a nonsmoking room as requested. The breakfast that is offered is fair, but Rue de Cler offers more.Rue de Cler was fun with its various stores still carefully displaying the winter fruits and vegetables, local fish, bread-- on tables in front of the shops.Reaching the hotel was easy by bus from the airport to the Opera Metro stop and then the purple line to L'Ecolie de Militaire. I would warn those with large bags that the Paris Metro does not have escalators going up and down, usually only up. Local attractions from the Hotel include a short ten minute walk from the Eiffel Tower and then catch the Hop on Hop off Red Bus. We have the Red Bus to be quick way to see the highlights of a city if you have limited time.Again-would highly recommend the Hotel Relais

<Author>tm68
<Content>Home away from home... I would like to start by stating that I have been to Paris many times, and found this little treasure of a hotel through America's favorite travel guide, Rick Steve's in his Paris 2007 guidebook. I called to make reservations, and the person on the other end was very fluent in English and very happy to take our reservation. It was the next day that we received an email from Relais-Bosquet thanking us for considering them, and to please let them know if we needed any help with dinner or tours. We accepted their help for dinner, and we were never disappointed. On the contrary, we were blown away. I have to say that as an American, name dropping goes a long way. When we showed up for dinner, and dropped Frederiques name from the hotel, they rolled out the carpet for us. I have to say that has never happened to me ever in Paris. The rooms are bright, spacious and have wonderful windows that open out. We had a beautiful view of the Eiffel Tower. There were two PC's in the lobby that had free high speed internet access. We were close to the metro and centrally located. There hotel is located in the quaint Rue Cler district. Just around the corner you are surrounded by bakeries, a fromagerie, a wine store, a market, a fruit market, and a chocolate shop. What more can you ask for? This hotel added to the whole Paris experience, because you could come home at night and ask all of the embarrassing questions without fear. We bought a phone card that had instructions only in French. The wonderful front desk person was so kind as to go through the whole auto-prompting and walked me through it. We will definitely go back to Paris, and the Relais-Bosquet will definitely be a part of our experience. Make sure you ask for Frederique...!!!

<Author>JBMaryland
<Content>Well run hotel I choose this hotel after reading reviews at Trip Advisor, and we weren't disappointed. It's a great location, close to the metro and walking distance to a number of sites, Eiffel Tower, Invalides, etc. There's a good sized supermarket nearby, tons of restaurants and cafes to choose from, and a great baker on the corner. The hotel staff was very friendly, and everyone spoke English.I was a little shocked by how tiny the room was, but it was clean and quiet. There was a second door to the hall that we closed at night, and there was an electric shutter on the windows to drown out sound and light from outside. This was a great feature as we had jet lag most of the week.There was free WIFI, a flat screened TV with some English language programs such as CNN and Skynews. There was a frig in the room, wine glasses and a corkscrew (which I thought was a nice touch). The maid service seemed to be invisible.We stayed 5 nights, and would have extended our stay another 2 nights, but the hotel was booked. We didn't realize how good we had it until we moved to a new hotel which was an absolutely horrible experience (and twice the price).

<Author>DJJones
<Content>Great Location - nice hotel The Hotel Relais Bosquet is just a stones throw from the Eiffel Tower. It is conveniently located for the Metro station at Les Invalides and you can be at any of the central Paris landmarks within 2 or 3 stops on the Metro or within 20 minutes if walking. The Hotel itself is clean, pleasant and represents good value for money. The rooms are not huge, but then this is Paris! The bathroom was functional and clean with a good range of complimentary toiletries and a hairdryer. The rooms also had irons and ironing boards as well as coffee making facilities and a mini-bar. The reception area downstairs was well appointed with complimentary newspapers (English and American) and free Internet access. The reception staff were helpful and knowledgeable. If you want a good standard hotel which is ideally placed then this is the Hotel for you. I would definitely return.  
<Date>Jan 17, 2008

<Author>vivelaweekend!
<Content>Lovely hotel and neighbourhood We checked in on a rainy friday early afternoon for a long weekend break and were delighted that the positive reviews for this hotel were very accurate. I have stayed in a few hotels in Paris before for both business and leisure and have found this one to be excellent value for money and based in a great neighbourhood.The hotel is based in 2 buildings (one behind the other, linked by a small corridor). The hotel is based on a quiet road, just 1 minute from Rue de Cler, a wonderful, bustling, pedestrianised street, full of fromageries, fine foods, fruit and veg shops, and cafes and restaurants (excellent choices for morning croissants and coffee). The hotel is 5 minutes walk from Ecole Militaire metro, which means there is only 1 change (at Srasbourg St Denis) if you are travelling on the Eurostar from Gare du Nord. Furthermore the hotel is only 10-15 minutes walk to the Seine and 2 minutes from Rue St.Dominique, with its good restaurants, boulangeries and shoe shops, that leads you down to the Boulevard St Germain with its upscale swanky shopping options.The hotel rooms are nicely decorated, clean and spacious, and ours, though it was on the top floor in the attic, didnt have a restrictive ceiling height. Our room had a plasma screen with satellite channels and a partial view of the Eiffel Tower (the tower's lights flash for 10 minutes on each hour during the night!) and a well stocked mini bar and tea/coffee facilities. The bathroom was clean and bright, with lush white fluffy towels provided, with the only mini-gripe being that the water pressure in the shower was rather low.The staff on the desk were very helpful with directions and restaurant recommendations, and very accommodating (they kindly stored our fromage in their fridge on our last day, until we were ready to leave).I would definitely recommend this hotel for anyone looking for good value for money and a quiet, central location.

<Author>edinburghedge
<Content>Many good things... and one bad. We booked our three night stay, Novermber 28-30, at the Relais Bosqueton Expedia.co.uk and got a terrific deal of 拢90 per night. I arrived at the hotel, (ahead of my other half travelling from Edinburgh), at approximately 8:00am after a flight from the United States. I was grateful for the effort made by the staff to get me into our room very early. Cab fare from Charles De Gaulle during morning rush hour was approximately 拢35. Room #45 is a standard room and for the most part it resembled the photo on the hotel's website. It was snug but not as small as some of the European rooms I've stayed in; we had no problem stashing our luggage out of the way. The view of the Eiffel Tower and the Rue du Champs de Mars, decorated for Christmas, was picture postcard pretty. The window was outfitted with an electric shutter which came in handy when we wanted to block out the noise from the street below. The room contained two small twin beds pushed together, a wooden wardrobe which stored an iron and ironing board andextra blankets, a small desk and chair, a mini bar with plenty of space to store our own water and snacks, and a working safe. Everything was clean and well presented. The bathroom was small but equipped with a full bath/shower and the standard ameneties. The towels were large and decent quality and there was plenty of hot waterand good water pressure at all times. One of the nicer things on offeris the use of the free internet access in the lobby. If you've never pecked out an e-mail on a French keyboard, (I hadn't), prepare to be amused. The hotel sits in a charming neighborhood with a range of goodcafes, bars and restaurants nearby. The Cafe Champs de Mars, just doors down from the hotel, was the perfect spot for a late meal after a night of pub crawling in Le Marais. The metro station and post office are within easy walking distance. The hotel staff both at reception and housekeeping are accomodating, friendly and professional. We didn't eat breakfast in the hotel so I can't comment on the food service. We enjoyed so many things about this wonderful little hotel but we did have one rather significant problem...we foundthe beds to be extremely uncomfortable. We loved the location, the price, the staff, the view, so many things...but we didn't sleep well.At the end of the day a good night's rest is the most important aspectof any hotel. We may choose this hotel again but we would certainly want to avoid the beds in room #45.

<Author>Travelgirl80
<Content>We felt like Parisians! This hotel is very charming, with the location being the greatest asset! We loved feeling like we were in a local area, with the street market and wonderful cafes around. Also, the metro stop is just around the corner so it is convenient to get other places as well. It is clean, with wonderful staff who were very helpful . The only problem we had was leaving at 4 a.m to catch a flight and trying to communicate with the night front desk clerk (his english was a lot more limited than other workers) as to why our taxi we had asked him to reserve was not there. We were getting frustrated, and unable to hail one that early in the morning, when he finally communicated to us that he had spoken with the company and one was on the way (although 45 min late). He zoomed us to the airport so it all worked out fine!The rooms are clean and sort of bed-and-breakfastish...not near as modern as all the other hotels we stayed at in Europe that had flat screens and modern furnishings but very clean and well taken care of. There was a strong smoke smell one night so we feared the place was on fire, but that same hotel clerk told us it was from another apartment next door or something.... The highlight of our room was the view! We requested an Eiffel Tower view so we could lay in bed and watch the Tower twinkle on the hour! This was one of the highlights of all of Europe for me! <Author>rebb6076
<Content>Great hotel;great location Our original plan was to stay at the Hotel Leveque on Rue Cler but I failed to properly confirm the reservation. We then selected the Relais Bosquet, and I am glad that we did. It is rather plain on the exterior but once inside, our room was very clean and well maintained. The room has a safe, small refrigerator and electronic window blinds that provided full room darkening. Best of all, we had a direct view of the Eiffel Tower from our room. It was great laying in bed and watching the twinkling light show. The hotel is a 15 minute walk to the Tower and the Seine. It is a half block from Rue Cler and the restaurants and shops (the bakery on the Corner of Rue Cler and Champ du Mars is better than the one adjacent to the hotel, in our opinion). The front staff spoke excellent English and were very helpful. In addition, there are two computers in the lobby with free access to the internet. This is a very useful tool to confirm or make reservations. The price per room was 160 euros. Well worth it in our opinion. We give this hotel as solid 5 for overall value and location. Highly recommended to others.

<Author>Baglady_NJ
<Content>Really Perfect at this price The Hotel Relais Bosquet is in a great location if you want to stay in a more local setting. Plenty of local resonable restauants (some quite good) and a great local food market right outside the door complete with one of the most famous cheese stores in Paris right across the street, called Ann Cantin (amazing) and Lenotre pastry around the corner.We had a superior room which was very nice. Comfortable bed, nice bathroom with double sink and seperate toilet. The room has a safe and a refrigerator which comes in handy being so close to the market. Also, you are less than two short blocks from metro and great location to walk to the Eiffel Tower.The staff was exceedingly helpful during day and Frederica is a standout for help. That said two comments on the slightly negative side. First, if you are a sophisticated eater and want advice on where to eat amazing French food I suggest you do your research and have the hotel make reservations. They are not very knowledgeable about food. Second, the hotel rate does not include breakfast which is an additional 13 euros per person (common in France). While I was there I found that if you mention Rick Steves and his travel books at the time of booking, breakfast is included, so this is a great tip and savings.We have booked again at the hotel for our next trip in 6 months and look forward to this reasonable hotel in crazy, expensive Paris.

<Content>Wonderful Stay at the Relais Bosquet My husband and I stayed here for part of our honeymoon in early September. The concierge was polite and helpful, the room was bright and cheerful with a lovely view out the window of the street below and the neighborhood was full of charming boutiques, restaurants, etc.There is an excellent bakery on the corner with wonderful quiche and pastries for breakfast (a better value than the hotel breakfast). <Author>henryv731_123
<Content>What A Gem! As most of the other reviews indicate, this hotel is simply a gem!!! I recommend it very, very highly.Tremendous location: 10 minutes from Eiffel Tower and Seine River cruises, 15 minutes from Orsay museum, 25 minutes from Louvre, and 35 minutes from Notre Dame. There are so many sites that are well within walming distance of the Relais Bosquet that its location is superb.If you get a chance, ask for a room with a view of the Eiffel Tower. It's trivial, but looking at your window to see the top of the tower leaves you with a memory yo won't soon forget.If you are a Rick Steves customer, tell the hotel. I mentioned that I discovered the hotel through Steves and they indicated that the continental breakfast was free for Steves' readers.Frederique, one of the clerks at the front desk, is incredibly friendly and helpful. Don't hesitate to ask her for help with getting a taxi, etc...A tip: if you are planning to visit museums in Paris, consider getting a museum pass. The hotel can arrange for this pass to be delivered to the hotel and waiting for you when you arrive, and it will allow you to by-pass lines that can sometimes be fairly lengthy.If you are staying at the Relais Bosquet, you are in for a treat. A great value and a great Parisian Hotel!

<Author>nealmosk
<Content>Wonderful little left bank hotel near the Rue Cler We loved absolutely everything about the place- no exageration. To start with, the covenient location: a block or so from the Rue Cler, where we could take nice little strolls away from the bulk of tourists, have a leisurely croissant and coffee in the morning or dejeuner at any of a number of eateries, and shop for our day at one of several marches, fromagerie, patisserie, bakeries, wine shop and deli, little book shops, etc. Also ATM machine across the street and Metro station (Ecole Militaire) a few blocks away, about half way between la Tour Eiffel and L'Hotel des Invalides by easy walking distance. The staff at the hotel were very friendly at any hour of day or night, spoke English but were willing to tolerate our broken French, and very helpful arranging touristy things for us. There is a computer with internet available and Wifi in the rooms. Also, well-stocked refrigerator, room service or breakfast downstairs if we needed (we did not with Rue Cler nearby), and very clean bathroom and toilet. It was a quaint and personal experience in a modern and well-equipped hotel. Will be staying there again on our next trip!

<Author>Mexifried
<Content>Good location, courteous staff, comfortable We have just returned from a 9 day stay at the Hotel Relais Bosquet and enjoyed ourselves thoroughly.We got to the hotel by Yellow Van which was arranged for us through the Hotel. This worked very well and made the transfer easy. You could have got here by a combination of the Roissy bus and Metro 8 but it would have involved hauling bags up and down quite a number of stairs. All in all, the van worked well and was not expensive.The front desk staff were extraordinarily helpful and pleasant. They speak excellent English and are happy to help you with suggestions, reservations and advice on request. Check in and out was efficient with no surprises.The front lobby has a computer to access the internet. It has a different keyboard than the one that we use in Canada but, with some considerable patience, you can get used to it. It is often used by guests but is generally available with a short wait. The hotel has wireless internet and so bringing a lap top would be a good idea.Ice is obtained through the front desk and isn't available on each floor which was fine as far as we were concerned.We had a superior room which was very nice. Had to insert the room key into a slot by the door to make the lights work, which was a new one for us and not something that came to us immediately. It had a large bathroom with two sinks and a large and effective shower. A separate WC was within the room. The air conditioning worked well, thank goodness! The safe was inside the small fridge (which wasn't the first place that we looked for it). The fridge has enough room to store soda, cheese, meat, and other stuff if you wish. They do stock it with the usual which we didn't use. They have a coffee maker in the room that we didn't use. There was a small TV which had 3 English channels plus a number of other channels. There was a large cabinet and a chest of drawers for clothes which was adequate. Electronically closing blinds completely darken the room and completely keep out outside noise. One could hear the doors open and close in adjacent hotel rooms.Breakfast was included in our package and was very good. It consisted of orange juice and cake to start, followed by coffee and heated milk, chocoate bread (addictive), croissants (very good) and additional bread with an assortment of jams and butter. Cheese came with it as did some cut up melon. This was one filling breakfast that was very good. We never were able to eat all of it and it pretty much filled you up until supper time cutting the costs of lunch (generally you might just need a drink and could share a salad and that would do you the rest of the day). I am sure that you could go out to a local bakery etc and it would be fine, but this was so convenient and so good!The hotel is about a 10 minute walk from the Eiffel tower and two blocks from the Metro. It is one block from Rue Cler. There are two bakeries nearby and two grocery stores as well. Banking was within two blocks.I highly suggest the Le Bosquet restaurant nearby as it has great service and food. Cafe du March is also close and is a little cheaper with reasonable food and a fun atmosphere. You can get a crepe on Rue Cler that is the equivalent of a full meal. Wine shops abound nearby. I highly recommend this hotel.  
<Date>Aug 8, 2007

<Author>Bunnytraveler
<Content>A Totally Wonderful Experience We traveled to Europe to celebrate our 40th anniversary and chose the Hotel Relais Bosquet for the Paris part of our trip. What a great choice! This hotel is situated in a lovely part of Paris close to so many things and just a few blocks from The Metro station so getting around the city was easy and convenient. I particularly loved seeing Parisians during their normal daily activities while sitting at a cafe or bistro on the Rue du Cler. I couldn't have asked for a better location or a more friendly and helpful staff. There is a computer in the lobby that you can use without charge (not a common occurrence in our experience overseas), a post office and laundromat just a few blocks away and you're blocks from the Eiffel Tower and the Seine. . .who could want anything more? I can't wait to get back for another visit fo Paris and will definitely stay at this hotel again anytime I'm in the city. I had high hopes when I left home and I was not disappointed! What a wonderful experience!!

<Author>emfdvm
<Content>Lovely Hotel and Neighborhood I can echo all of the previous reviewers comments. I stayed here with my 9-year-old daughter for the weekend and we found it to be a really nice hotel in a charming area. It was very convenient to the Metro and tourist attractions and there were ample choices for eating very close by. If there is one caveat I would add, it is that this hotel seems very popular with, and populated by, Americans. We didn't spend much time there, except to sleep, so we didn't interact much within the hotel, but if you want a real Parisian experience surrounded by people from all over, this may not be for you. Given my limited French and our short stay, it was perfect for us.On a second note: I was determined to do the entire weekend using only public transportation, as there was only 2 of us. The trip from CDG by train and Metro took about 1 hour, involved 2 transfers (from RER to Metro and then once within the Metro), and cost 8.10 euro in and 9.50 euros out (per person). We had only carryon bags, but if we had had larger luggage, it would have been difficult. If I were to do it again, I would recommend taking the RER or a shuttle to a central Paris location, then getting a cab to the hotel from there. With a larger number of people, a cab all the way from the airport might be the best option.

<Author>PharmDoc
<Content>What at great location. This is our second time back to the Hotel Relais Bosquet thanks to Rick Steves. It is a little scarey to walk around the area and see Rick Steves' Paris travel guide in most everyone's hand.However, he is right; the location is great. You can walk to either corner to get great pastry to eat in your room with the coffee provided or just walk to the Rue Cler and eat breakfast while the market is set up. You have an ATM across the street and a small grocery a few doors down. If you stay long enough to need clean clothes, you don't have far to walk to a clean laundromat. No one can complain about the size of the bathrooms which are larger than most we have encountered in Europe. We had a smaller room this time, but still facing the courtyard which keeps the street noise to a minimum. Fredricka scheduled a shuttle for the two of us from CDG to the hotel for 36E which isn't as cheap as the metro, but with luggage, it is considerably easier. Oh, you internet geeks, like my husband, they now have WiFi in the rooms. They also have a computer in the lobby for free use if you need to check your e-mail. This place has the basics and is close to everything. No doubt we would go back again.

<Author>plmguy61
<Content>Lovely place We just returned from our trip and a wonderful stay at Relais Bosquet. It's as charming and friendly a place as you could ask fort, and in a great location. Our room was spotless and spacious, with all the amenities we could want, including a safe and a mini-bar. It also had very handy electric blinds that could be lowered, which was a big help, since it stayed light surprisingly late there. There was also an internet terminal in the lobby for checking e-mail , and free newspapers in French and English.Frederica and Christian were incredibly helpful with everything, including dinner reservations, taxis, and anything else we needed.The Rue Cler neighborhood where the hotel is located is a nice quiet spot, but very well situated. You can walk to quite a bit (You're especially close to the Eiffel Tower and the Invalides) and there is a Metro station (Ecole Militaire) only about a 5 minute walk away. There are two wonderful bakeries within a block of the hotel (one practically downstairs), and we got pastries for our breakfast most days. There is also a small grocery store just a few steps away, and many other food shops and produce stands very close. The hotel serves a continental breakfast, but it was not included with our room and was a little pricey (15 euros a person), so we did not eat there. There are also several cafes very close at hand where you can sit down for a breakfast and watch the world go by.

<Author>CAOItalia
<Content>My new Paris home! This hotel is an excellent find! I've stayed in the Rue Cler area the last three times Ive been to Paris, and the Relais Bosquet tops the other two places that I've stayed. I love this little neighborhood and it feels like I'm living in Paris when I stayed here. This was our 1st anniversary trip and my wife's first time in Paris, and she felt the same way. Rooms are nicely sized, the air-conditioning is good, and the hotel staff is so accomodating. Special kudos to Christian for his assistance on this trip. The hotel is just off of Avenue Bosquet, and the location is great for walking to numerous sights and some excellent restaurants; Les Clos du Gourmets, La Cuisine, and Venezia Italia. We had an inside room that overlooked a courtyard and it was very quiet. I highly recommend this hotel and this neighborhood in general. If you're a foodie, it may take you a couple of days to get past all the great shops. (You're right across the street from Marie-Anne Cantin--one of Paris' best cheese shops.) You're just a few blocks from the Eiffel Tower. We got there at 9:15 on Sunday morning with practically no one in the individuals line, and we were in the first car up. No downside to this hotel or location at all. But skip the 13 Euro breakfast, and hit the boulangerie down the corner to the right as you leave the hotel.

<Author>ann99bray
<Content>Loved the Relais Bosquet, Great Location We stayed at the Relais Bosquet for a week this month. We found the recommendation for the hotel in Rick Steve's guidebook. We were not disappointed. We had a nice size room for Paris and an unusually large bathroom for Europe with 2 sinks. Everything was spotless. The hotel has air conditioning which was great as it was really hot for April. Our room had a small refrigerator which was useful for storing water, wine and cheese. We loved the location. About a 10 minute walk from the Eiffel Tower and round the corner from Rue Cler with its open markets and cafes and restaurants. The hotel is a few minutes walk from the Ecole Militaire metro (line 8) and bus #69 stops nearby (great route - Invalides, Musee D'Orsay, Louvre, near Notre Dame and Marais) and a few mintues from bus stop #92 (Arch de Triomphe and Gare Montparnasse (we went to the latter to catch a train for Chartres). We used the buses a lot as the routes were so direct and it gave us a chance to see more of Paris but they can be hot in warm weather - no air conditioning! The staff at the hotel were efficient and friendly - both the front desk staff and Barbara who serves a nicely presented continental breakfast with yummy fresh strawberries. The hotel also has free internet in the lobby. The room has an iron, hair dryer, wine glasses and wine opener and coffe/tea maker. One thing to watch for - if the hotel calls a taxi for you, the charge will start from the time the cab leaves the taxi stand. We got a taxi to the airport and when it arrived there was already about 9.70 euros on the meter. This is not the case if you flag down a cab on the street. We were glad we choose this area of Paris as other areas like the Marais seemed so crowded and it was nice to come back to the green boulevards and see the Eiffel Tower, especially lit up at night. We had a wonderful time in Paris and would definetely come back to the Relais Bosquet and not hestiate to recommend it.

<Author>Noakesi
<Content>C'est Fantastique! Having read the reviews following a Paris ratings search within our specified budget; I'd say we came up trumps with the Hotel Relais Bosquet.I booked the hotel for a short inexpensive break to Paris to celebrate our first anniversary; and found the hotel to be relaxed, very friendly and helpful. We only stayed the one night, and given our limited time chose to be out and about more than in; for which the hotel via the efficient metro system is in easy reach of anything you need to see and do (the Eiffel tower is in walking distance and we easily got to principle sites within aprx 25 minutes tops - all times of day/night).The room was spacious, clean and airy.We chose not to have breakfast in the hotel, rathermore chose to turn right out of the hotel and onto Rue Cler for on a Sunday a thriving local scene full of cafes and small shops selling a wonderful array of cheeses, fish, meat, vegetables  fruit and of course bread and pastries. Wonderful.We would visit again without hesitation and would glady recommend it to friends and family.Getting to the hotel is very straightforward from Roissy Charles de Gaulle. RER 'B' to Chatelet les Halles. Change to Metro line 1 (Yellow) heading west to La Defense; changing at Concorde to Metro line 8 heading south to Balard - alighting three stops down at Ecole Militaire. Easy.

<Author>larover
<Content>Nice Hotel In Great Area This is the third hotel I have stayed at in Paris and it offers great bang for the buck. It is not grand but the rooms (we had the superior) are quite spacious for Paris and well appointed. The roll down shades which block out all the light are a nice feature as is the in room tea/coffee maker, iron and ironing board and mini bar with room for your own items. The hotel is quite pleasant and homey and while you will have a comfortable bed don鈥檛 expect down pillows. In fact my only criticism is that like many of the boutique hotels in Paris there was no option but somewhat uncomfortable foam pillows.The staff is very friendly and although I speak French they speak fairly good English. Breakfast was tasty鈥︹€aker鈥檚 basket with bread, croissant, chocolate croissant, fresh squeezed orange juice, cake, small package of cheese and unlimited coffee and tea. It is worth it if you drink a fair amount of coffee or tea in the morning as these are quite pricey at restaurants in Paris and you will pay for refills at those cafes, bistros or restaurants. You can also have ham and fresh cheese a boiled egg or cereal for a few euros more.What really makes this hotel is the decent room size coupled with the area. As many posters have pointed out you are right near Rue Cler and in a residential area of Paris. You therefore can go to local cheeses shops, bakeries, etc and feel like a part of a neighborhood as you will see many Parisians doing the same thing. There are also many good restaurants nearby on Rue St Dominique and a few other local streets. There is somewhat of a nightlife if what you are looking for is a late night caf茅 scene and you will meet locals at those cafes. If you are looking for a bustling club scene night life I don鈥檛 think it is in this area. You are also quite close to the Metro and SNCR/RER for other areas outside of Paris. After we left the hotel we spent 2 nights at The Intercontinental Grand Hotel. In contrast the Grand is as it鈥檚 name implies Grand. However it is right in the midst of a tourist area where I don鈥檛 think you experience the true Paris and you will pay through the nose for everything you might want although it will be expertly provided for you.The Relais Bosquet on the other hand had everything you might reasonably require in a great setting and area. I would stay here again without hesitation and think it is a very nice value for the money. As an aside we did pass Le Walt Hotel which is very close by and seemed online to be nicer but more expensive. They were booked so we stayed at Relais Bosquet. I鈥檓 glad we did. Le Walt sits on a busy street and the rooms are supposedly quite small. It did not seem worth the extra money. In fact I am not aware of a hotel I would rather stay at in this area over Relais Bosquet.Oh and don't forget to try the bread at the bakery next door as well as at the corner of Rue Bosquet and Rue Cler.

<Content>Great apartment, professional staff We stayed 5 nights at the one-bedroom apt managed by the hotel. The apt's half a block from the hotel on a very quiet street on the ground level. The front desk staff offered adequate service for a 3-star hotel. With that said, I鈥檇 like to command the hotel staff on their professional and courteous way of handling problems. We encountered a problem with the apt lock upon check-out. One of the keys was stuck in the lock and we were unable to open the door. The hotel manager and staff calmly helped us check out and allowed us to leave for airport. We were told that the deposit would probably have to be forfeited if the hotel incurred costs in fixing the situation. I was not optimistic that I would be able to get much of the deposit back. However, the hotel emailed me after a couple days and let me know the cost was 30 euros. I was relieved to learn that it wasn鈥檛 a costly problem and the hotel staff handled it promptly and kept us informed. I鈥檇 go for a hotel if it鈥檚 your first time in Paris and prefer to join tours and visit the city in a well-planned out way. I鈥檇 recommend the apartment to experienced travelers who are adventurous and willing to find their ways around Paris. Staying at the apt is a bit more costly than staying at a hotel but it鈥檚 all worth it. It was very nice to be able to come back to a 鈥渉ome-like鈥?environment after being out and about for a long day.

<Author>Jasmine13
<Content>Lovely, quiet honeymoon stay My husband and I just returned from our honeymoon in France this week. Our stay at Relais Bousquet was, for the price, the most comfortable, clean, and well-located accommodation of the trip. The room was tastefully decorated with important amenities: mini bar, tv, water heater for tea, a bathroom with 2 sinks and a nice enough shower/tub combo so that I could enjoy evening baths. After leaving the Relais Bousquet, we hit the road for Normandy and it was not until then that we realized how nice our Paris accommodations had been for the money. We stayed at a number of hotels that were a bit less expensive or quite a bit more expensive, and none of them to me were as comfortable as the room we had at the Relais Bousquet. The location was excellent: within walking distance to the Eiffel tower or across the bridge to the Right Bank, Trocadero; superb neighborhood restaurants on Rue le Dominique; and great transportation with the Metro  convenient 69 bus. Breakfast was adequate at the hotel, but just as easy to walk 2 minutes to Rue Cler and pick up something a little tastier. Also, the Super Marche is right next door to the Relais Bousquet which was very convenient.

<Author>LonelyAvenue
<Content>Excellent hotel with great staff and a good location My wfe, mysefl and daughter stayed at Hotel Relais Bosquest twice during the quiet Paris month of August 2006. The hotel staff, Gerard  Abel, was exceptional. They were on all occassions extremely polite, professional and helpful. The Hotel is situated in a real middle to upper middle-class neighborhood, a short distance from Invalides and the Eiffel Tower. It is one block from the gourmet corridor known as Rue Cler. There are artisanal cheese shops and bolangerie one block in eash direction. A post office is around the corner. The metro is one block away. There is an ATM at the bank right across the street; a supermarket three doors donw ; a dry cleaner next to that; a self-service laundromat one block east and some lovely inexpenseive brasseries within footsteps of the hotel. Of course, you can easily get to St . Germain and all the other areas of Paris quickly and efficiently via the metro. The Relais Bosquet offers free internet and wifi in its lobby and a breafast, which we did not take advantage of. The rooms  beds were very comfortable and clean, some with balconies providing a view of Paris roof tops and the Eiffel Tower. We would most certainly stay at the Hotel Relais Bosquet again. Gerard at the front desk was particularly helpful. (By the way, if you have not been to Paris previously or in a long time, I recommend you walk over the the Seine, right beyond the Eiffel Tower some nice evening and take the river tour cruise - corny, but it definitely helps you to begin to appreciate the overwhelming beauty, age and history of the city).

<Author>travelngurl
<Content>Great experience!! A friend and I stayed here just recently for a week. I was familiar with the Rue Cler area and really liked the quiet residential feel. I chose this hotel based on trip advisor and found that it had also been recommended by Rick Steves. We had booked a standard room on the 5th floor on the street side (all the superior rooms were booked) and it was pretty good size (by european standards) for the two of us. I asked for an upper floor and a view of the eiffel tower and they did not disappoint me. What a fantastic view each evening to see it lit up (or twinkling on the hour) outside your window when you return to your room!!! I ducked my head into a room that was a 'superior' and I would recommend spending the extra $$ for the extra room it provided.Yes, I will admit, this does not look like a new hotel as based on the furnishings. And, yes, I think I saw a bath towel that was frayed a bit. But I thoroughly enjoyed my stay. Everyone who worked there was more than friendly at all times. They answered all our questions with a smile. And opened our wine bottle when we realized the cork was REALLY stuck in there!! Who can ask for more? And they recommended a REALLY great restaurant on the next street over La Litote on Rue Bosquet which is a definite MUST for anyone staying in the 7th!The rooms are nicely decorated (bright yellow in our room) and it is really clean (which is a big issue for me). Although halfway through the week we must have had a change in the cleaning woman and we could tell as it wasn't cleaned as well. But still more than sufficient.Breakfast is free if you mention Rick Steves. Hey, I though you get a good deal for what you got---and hey, its free!! If you want more variety for breakfast, yes, Rue Cler is around the corner but I was happy with my croissant and coffee. (you get more than that)The roll down shades are great! Really gives you a great nights sleep. Air conditioner worked great and there is a safe in the room. I would highly recommend this place to anyone and would stay there again in a minute.

<Author>Judsongirl
<Content>Great Hotel  Had a very good experience with this hotel. We stayed here over the first week in July and booked the hotel a couple of months before we left. Unfortunately, no Eiffel Tower views were available -- we knew that when we made our reservations -- and our windows faced the courtyard. We paid EUR147.00 a night. Hotel was very, very prompt in answering emails.The Hotel Relais Bosquet is located in a less touresty area of the 7th arrondissement. The Hotel is only a couple of blocks from the Metro -- best way to travel in Paris. Best of all, the rooms are air conditioned with individual controls!!!!!!! Definitely a plus when the weather in Europe has been so odd the past couple of years.I was concerned when we saw our room because it was next to the elevator. No worries. Couldn't hear a thing (I made my husband test it before I unpacked).Windows had, best I can describe, hurricane shutters that you could electronically lower if you liked. They blocked out 100% of the light. I had the best sleep I have had in a very long time. Room had a safe and a small refrigerator. Bath had double sinks and a tub/shower combo. Separate room off bath held toilet. Room was normal size -- and large by Euro standards. I've stayed in smaller in the States. This is not a new hotel and one should not expect it to look like one. But I found the room clean, maid service excellent, and the management helpful. Don't bother with eating breakfast at the hotel because the rue Cler is just about half a block away, and a bakery next door. Lots of food (baked goods, crepes, fruit, wine, and cheese) at this open air market area. Check out their web site. I found the pictures of the hotel were accruate. We will most definitely stay here again.

They advertise a free breakfast if you mention the guide book, but don't expect too much.As soon as we walked into the lobby, we were disappointed to note the rather worn and dirty carpet. Once up in our room, we noticed the carpet had not been vacuumed there either. The furniture looks like it has seen its share of travelers. It is mismatched and badly beaten furniture. We were afraid to sit on the ottoman at the foot of the bed, the legs were so bent in they looked like they would cave in from our weight. The two chairs in our room were just as bad with the framing making them very uncomfortable to sit in. The towels were nice and clean, but badly frayed.We had mixed results with the receptionists. One receptionist when asked about a Paris map, couldn't find one for us. When asked again about tours of Paris, he was unable to find any information for us. A couple of nights later, we had a new receptionist who was very helpful. When we told him about our previous requests to his co-worker, he was like a magician and pulled out maps and several Paris tour books for our use.And to our surprise, one evening on returning from a day of sight seeing, the lobby carpet had been cleaned during our absence. But the funny thing is, the travel guide who I have mentioned above, just happened to be in Paris while we were there and his associates were doing inspections and updating their travel guide books for next year.However, we did have a spectacular view of the Eiffel Tower from our room.My recommendation is to pay more for a room elsewhere and buy a croissant at the local patisserie.

<Author>sue7778
<Content>Charming hotel near Rue Cler I was travelling with 6 other people and we were all staying near Rue Cler. Most hotels are small and book quickly. The hotels where others were staying were booked. That's how I came across this gem of a hotel.The front desk staff is very professional and treated us very well. They were accomodating when we asked them to make dinner reservations for our party of 7. The room was very clean and comfortable and had air conditioning. The windows have privacy shades which keeps light out and reduces street noise (I heard no street noise at all). The shades are on the exterior and are operated by a click of a button (by the bed). There is a coffee maker with free coffee, and a mini-bar (at fairly reasonable rates). There is a dresser, desk, armoire, and TV in the room. There is internet access in the breakfast room, which is free for guests. It is not attached to a printer, so if you need to print something, you will need to go elsewhere.The hotel is about a minutes walk from the Rue Cler pedestrian street. This street has a couple of cafes, a delicious crepe/Greek restaurant, and many other shops. There are two grocery stores within the block and a couple of bakeries. We never ate breakfast at the hotel because there we opted to eat outside at a cafe or ate on the run (being late to meet our family/friends).The hotel is a few minutes walk from the subway (only one subway line stops at Ecole Militaire).It is an easy walk to the Eiffel Tower and it was fun to walk over there in the evening and watch the light show and people.I would definitely stay at this hotel again. It was an excellent stay!

<Author>Tara3056
<Content>Loved the Relais Bosquet!!! My husband and I stayed at the Relais-Bosquet for 7 nights in January of this year. I was a little hesitant about booking a regular double room (as opposed to a superior double) because we'd never been to Europe before and had heard nothing but horror stories about the small rooms. I needn't have worried! The room, while cozy, was plenty large enough for the two of us and our two big suitcases (+ carry on backpack and shoulder bag). We didn't feel like we were stepping all over each other, or our luggage.The room had an armoire where we could hang some of our clothes, iron and ironing board, those wonderful electric darkness blinds, and a very functional bathroom with hairdryer and nice toiletries. Oh, and there was also a safe and mini-fridge. You could buy items from the mini-bar, but it also came in handy for us to store our own sodas/water. Just walk a few steps to the right of the hotel's front door, to the grocery store there, and buy Coke or Evian for something like 2.50-3.00 Euros for a 6 pack of either.The front desk staff was always warm and helpful, and housekeeping was excellent. I do recommend that you tip the housekeeper each day - it's apparently the norm in Europe, and you'll get much better service if you do it each day instead of waiting until the end of your stay. I generally left 2-3 Euros a night, and in return, got extra toiletries and towels, a spotlessly clean room, AND I wasn't charged for the 2 drinks we actually did take from the mini-bar before realizing we could just walk to the grocery store.We really enjoyed using the free internet on the computer in the breakfast room. I was able to check in with friends and family, and also get info about some of the tourist sites we wanted to visit later in our trip.The carpet and furniture in the lobby and in the halls is slightly worn, but we didn't mind at all. For the price and location, this hotel is a GEM.As for location, you couldn't ask for better. We spent some time in the Latin Quarter at night, and it was bustling and noisy even late at night. We really loved coming home to our little section of Paris, where it was peaceful and not as crowded. At the same time, it was soooo easy to get from our location in the 7th to anywhere else in Paris. For one, Paris is incredibly walk-able. Second, the Ecole Militaire metro stop is an easy 3 minutes or so away. I was a bit intimidated to try using the metro on our first day, but it really was easy, and we ended up using it multiple times a day, zipping all over Paris with ease. Finally, the location can't be beat for restaurants. The 7th is full of lovely little bistros that are moderately priced (23-30 Euros per person for a delicious multi-course prix fixe meal). In short, the Relais Bosquet is fabulous, and I'm fairly certain that if you choose you stay there, you will love it as much as we did!

<Author>smokey1127
<Content>Pleasant Hotel We stayed at Hotel Relais Bosquet for a week in June 2006 and were thoroughly satisfied. We were able to check in early, which was appreciated after the long flight. The staff was gracious and accomodating. They helped us with our French and spoke excellent English as well. We selected a superior room with Eiffel Tower view. The bathroom was clean and modern, although we did have a slightly claustrophobic separate WC. The bed was actually two singles put together with some sort of a bridge to eliminate the gap. It was comfortable if a bit firm. We were grateful for the air conditioning on the warmer days. The mini-fridge was convenient for storing goodies purchased at the wonderful shops nearby. There were many, boutiques and restaurants within easy walking distance of the hotel. The only downside of the location was that the closest subway line didn't run directly to many major attractions. All this meant was changing lines, so it really wasn't a problem and certainly wouldn't deter us from staying in the area on our next visit.We loved the neighborhood! We had considered other areas, namely the Marais and St. Germaine de Pres, but we were certain the Rue Cler area was the right choice after visiting the others. It just felt like a real neighborhood. We had breakfast daily at Cafe du Marche on the corner, and we came to recognize the locals dining and walking by. By the end of the trip we even managed to coax a smile out of the crusty tabac shopkeeper.Thanks to the many previous reviewers whose insights helped us select Hotel Relais Bosquet!
