<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful Hotel This hotel is an absolute gem! My friend and I arrived in Paris on a rainy Sunday afternoon. We had reserved a room for four nights at a nearby hotel that turned out to be nothing like what was represented on the hotel's website on in France for Dummies. We called back to the US and had my husband check TripAdvisor for some other hotels in the same neighborhood. With three hotel names in hand, we wandered out in the rain and happily found the Hotel Relais-Bosquet just two blocks away. We walked into the lobby, looking quite soggy and miserable, and inquired if they had a room available. The man at the front desk was so kind and polite when we explained that we had a reservation at another hotel but the room was unsatisfactory. He said he had a room we could have for two nights but then we would have to change to a different room. We were more than happy to change rooms since we did not have a reservation. The desk clerk then asked us if we would like to see the room. It was lovely -- spacious, clean and beautifully decorated. We immediately went back to the other hotel, checked out and returned to the Relais-Bosquet with our luggage. As soon as we walked up to the desk, the clerk told us that he had found a room that we could have for all four nights. We checked in and went to the room. While it was a bit smaller than the first room, it was still very comfortable and spacious. The bathroom was very spacious as well and spotlessly clean. We had drawer space, armoire space and lots of shelf space in the bathroom. After getting settled in our room, we went to the lobby to check our e-mail since we hadn't been near a computer in a week. We asked the desk clerk if he could recommend a restaurant for dinner. He told us that many places were closed on Sunday and especially this particularly Sunday because Monday was May 1, a national holiday. He said, Let me see if I can get a reservation for you. He called several places and did arrange reservations for dinner at a very nice, reasonably priced restaurant about 10 mins. away. This was the beginning of a beautiful friendship between us and the people at the front desk. Every single one of them was so polite and helpful. They made reservations for us for all types of things and kept us apprised of when the museums were open, the best times to visit different sites, etc. We enjoyed the breakfast every morning we were there. The breakfast room is very light and airy and the service by Christian was impeccable. Whenever I return to Paris, I will stay at this lovely hotel.  
<Date>May 16, 2006

<Author>gbtrotter
<Content>No Better Place to Stay in Paris Great location, great price, great rooms - what more can you ask for?We arrived tired and hungry at the hotel at 11:00am. Our room was ready as was a recommendation for lunch nearby. The room was clean, comfortable and large by Paris standards. Checking email on the lobby computer downstairs, free of charge, was a great plus as was the view of the Eiffel Tower from our window. The Rue Cler neighborhood is perfect for anyone - couples, families, etc. There are two bakeries are at either corner on the same block as the hotel. A market is just a few doors down if you need something, but only if all the shops and street vendors have closed shop on Rue Cler. Of course, there are about 50 cafes and restaurants within a five block radius of the hotel. Try La Petit Troquet or La Florimond (both non-smoking).You are a five minute walk from the Ecole Militaire Metro station and a ten minute walk from the Eiffel Tower. In addition to all the usual sites, we had a great time on two tours with Fat Tire Tours in Paris, also within walking distance of the hotel. One was a segway tour of the city which lasted about four hours. We were treated like celebrities and asked to stop for pictures all along the way. The other great tour was a bike tour to Versailles - you bike from the office near the Eiffel Tower to a nearby train station, train to Versailles, stop at a market to pick up items for a picnic and bike around Versailles - definitely the best way to see its 800 acres. We ended the day with an audio tour of the chateau. They have many other tours as well including walking tours of several neighborhoods and evening bike tours.

<Content>A charming little hotel We had a fantastic 6 days stay in Paris and it is really wonderful to be able to come back to a comfortable hotel room, after a long day of tripping around Paris, to relax before venturing out into the cold in search of a place for dinner.There are plenty of restaurants to choose from nearby without having to go too far afield. <Author>MikkiBlau
<Content>A Masterpiece in Paris You will not find another hotel like this in Paris at the same affordable price. Everything about this hotel is unbeatable. The room was large enough to move around in and relaxingly appointed in bright, airy golden tones. And no squeezing into a tiny, sparsely lit bathroom; this bathroom was clearly remodeled recently and was impeccably clean, with bathtub/shower combination and lots of light. The best part about this hotel is the staff. From the minute I made my reservation to the time I checked out, we received nothing but courteous and friendly service, all delivered with a smile. And feel free to communicate with them by email! They are attentive and responsive to questions or concerns. In addition, they are quite knowledgable and more than prepared to offer whatever advice the new (or returning!) traveller to Paris needs. The lounge area in the lobby even sports recent editions of some of the popular city travel guides to Paris. They offer a continental breakfast, but we did not try it.The other fabulous part about this hotel is it's location. It is on a cosy side street just 5 minutes walk from the Ecole Militaire Metro station. With the Tour Eiffel, shops, varied restaurants, a market, and drugstore right there at it's doorstep, one doesn't have to go far to satisfy whatever needs come up.I have stayed in many hotels around Europe. Hotel Relais Bosquet is the first to cover ALL the essentials of a perfect stay!

<Author>090909
<Content>Extra Amenities, Perfect Location My husband and I stayed at Hotel Relais Bosquet October 2005 for 3 nights during our first stop on a 3-week journey through Europe. The hotel was 150 euros/night (about $180 US) and did not include breakfast. We were very pleased with the hotel overall and will stay here when we return and will also recommend to friends. Here's a rundown ...Spacious (by Europe's standards) modern bathrooms with plush towels and wash clothes - a rare luxury in Europe; spotless rooms that were well-maintained and cleaned daily; professional, helpful English-speaking staff; terrific location (right next to Rue Cler, which is the pedestrian-friendly food market, so delicious food is a stone's throw away); best boulangerie in Paris for breakfast and for patisseries (located on the corner across from delicious Cafe du Marche, which serves excellent Parisian cafe fare for reasonable prices); hotel is located a short 5-minute walk to the Eiffel Tower; free Internet access in the lobby; quiet neighborhood (request a room facing the courtyard for maximum quiet); black-out blinds, which would be helpful during the summer months.The hotel charges 6.5 euros/person additional for a standard, uninspiring continental breakfast, which is served in their lobby. I would recommend forgoing this expense and instead visiting the boulangerie for delicious breads and pastries and then walking 5 more steps to Cafe du Marche to sit and enjoy your breakfast and order coffee, juices, etc. at the cafe.Although the room was a bit expensive, we were happy with the extra amenities Hotel Relais Bosquet affords. Many US travelers might find the size of the rooms very small by US standards, but these rooms are fairly large by Europe standards and the bathrooms are especially large and modern. If you want to stay in this perfect Paris neighborhood but are on budget, try Champ du Mars, which is located 2 doors down from Relais Bosquet. We met several travelers who were staying there and were very happy with this hotel (its rate was less than 100 euros/night). Otherwise, stay at Relais Bosquet for a terrific experience.  
<Date>Oct 23, 2005

<Author>chewpei
<Content>small room, but very comfortable We stayed here for 5 nights and grew to appreciate the hotel more the longer we stayed. Our first impression wasn't great -- the halls were dirty and the standard room was very small. The bathroom was fairly large. But we loved the neighborhood -- lots of places to eat, close to the metro, close to the Eiffel Tower, convenient to stores for food, and we felt very safe walking at night too (we were a mother and teenage daughter this trip). The a/c is a basic we take for granted in the US, but much appreciated for being able to close the windows and block street noise even. We loved the room darkening blinds especially since it was light past 10 p.m. in July. It was nice to have a minibar fridge big enough for our morning juice (we didn't have breakfast at the hotel -- didn't look like much either). The halls were cleaned every other day it seemed, but the room was always kept very clean and the bathroom was well stocked and clean as well. The staff was helpful -- some more than others. It was funny to see all the Americans in the neighborhood with their Rick Steves' books! One piece of advice -- don't take his Roissy bus/metro suggestion for getting to the hotel. It took us almost three hours to get there as the bus was late and then drove around the airport for a half hour picking up more people, and then drove through city traffic for over an hour. The hotel recommended a shuttle which we took back to the airport and they were great. Try Pizza Tina for dinner.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>This hotel may be unsafe for women travelling alone! On July 6, 2005 I arrived from dinner at 12:30 am to my hotel, Hotel Relais Bosquet. I had been at this hotel for 9 days visiting my daughter in Paris. This is the 4th visit to this wonderful neighborhood hotel that is very pretty with a very lovely staff. That evening the night desk clerk became very agressive upon my arrival. He pulled me into the basement kitchen to get wine from the refrigerator. I managed to get back up the stairs. He then tried to come to my room. I quickly went up the stairs to the room of a friend and her son to learn that his behavior toward her had been much the same. The next morning I, along with my female friend and her son who were also guests in the hotel, filed a formal written complaint against the actions of the night desk clerk with the hotel manager. We learned that he had worked there for 4 years. The hotel sent both of us roses and champagne as an apology. On the early evening of July 7, the manager asked all of us to confront this man with our written complaints in both English and French. He began to scream at me and call me a liar. I left the area and called American Express to assist me to find another hotel immediately. The hotel did not fired this man. I had reservations to return to the hotel July 14 for 3 nights. The hotel suggested I go elsewhere because he would be remaining in employment there. The hotel did not charge me for my last 2 nights at the hotel. The hotel did not charge the other woman and her son for 2 nights, also. We both checked out on July 8 and did not return the next week as planned.I consider this an unsafe hotel for women who may be travelling with another female friend, son or daughter, or alone. It makes me very sad because I have loved the hotel and the location. I moved to the Intercontinental Hotel for the return to Paris.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the hotel, but disappointed with service! We just returned from a 5 day stay in Paris and we had a wonderful time! The weather was a little chilly, but overall it was a great trip! We stayed at the Relais Bosquet and were pleasantly surprised at how nice the rooms were! They were spacious, and the bathroom was large  clean. The towels were a good size, and the shower had good water pressure and warm water through the entire shower! Only problem we had was the shower curtain clinging to your body as you showered, but that is minor! However, after reading so many positive reviews regarding the hotel staff, we were disappointed with our experience. We did not feel that the staff was helpful and welcoming. Many of them would look down at their computer and busy themselves as we walked in rather than having to speak to us. They always said Bonjour, but did not look like they wanted to deal with us other than that. When we did have questions, they answered them, but never went beyond that. I had emailed some questions in advance, and my email was never acknowledged. Overall, we felt that the hotel staff was the least friendly and helpful people that we encountered in Paris. We had expected much more! That being said, we still enjoyed our stay at the Relais Bosquet, and would recommend it to anyone based on the quality of the rooms and the location. We loved walking down to Rue Cler to get our breakfast every morning at the corner patisserie. We had a great meal at Cafe du Marche down the street. The hotel was a short walk to the Eiffel Tower, Metro stop, RER stop, and other sights. Definately a convenient location and a pleasant neighborhood!

<Author>markandjulie
<Content>Je t'aime Paris! My husband and I spent 4 nights at the Relais Bosquet. From our 5th floor window we could see the top of the Eiffel Tower. The hotel is convenient, charming, and the staff was very warm and inviting. Our room had a refrigerator and electric room-darkening shades which my husband loved! There is free internet service in the lobby. The Rue Cler district is great - with fresh fruits, vegetables, breads, cheese, chocolates, etc. just steps from the front door of the hotel. The 7th arrondisment is a very nice neighborhood. It is just a short walk to the Eiffel Tower, Les Invalides, and Ecole Militaire metro stop. We even walked from our hotel to Notre Dame and the Louvre! The hotel arranged shuttle service from CDG airport for us. A great find!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Should we tell you? We recently stayed at THE RELAIS BOSQUET and had a wonderful few daysThe rooms were spacious by French standard,the beds very comfortable and the ensuite clean light and airy and the towels changed every day.Unlike most medium priced hotels in Paris we had tea and coffee facilities and a fridge and a superb view of the Eiffel Tower illuminated at night.We ate out for breakfast a couple of mornings but then decided to try breakfast in the hotel. It was the best we had and although it appears expensive it was cheaper than other places because you were not paying for coffee by the cup. It was a very good continental breakfast and lasted us all day.So don`t be put off.There were many good restaurants around to suit all pockets and we found the staff very knowledgeable about places to eat. The staff were very helpful on all sorts of matters and we thought this hotel was a real find.It`s also superblysituated for the Metro and bus service.Please don`t tell too many people about it or else we won`t get in next year. We really enjoyed APRIL IN PARIS 2005

<Author>GroovyYaYa
<Content>Can't wait to go back... I stayed at the Hotel Relais Bosquet in October 2004 with my family - what a wonderful hotel, in a fantastic location. I had the opportunity to stay in two different rooms - first night with a cousin that was able to be with us for a day and a night, then I moved into a 3 bed room with my folks to save money. Both rooms were very clean, very comfortable (even the rollaway I was on). We could see the upper half of the Eiffel Tower from our room, and the Rue Cler was a wonderful place to try local foods to create a picnic, or even buy a sandwich to put in your backpack (to eat on a sightseeing bus or outside somewhere in between sights). The Eiffel Tower is definitely within walking distance (good place to catch the hop-on, hop off buses) A metro stop is also conveniently nearby.I would definitely stay here again if I have the opportunity to visit Paris again.

<Author>klf0963
<Content>Wonderful Trip Just returned from a long weekend at the Bosquet. The hotel was very clean and comfortable. The double (king, I think) bed was firm -- great after a long day of sightseeing. The location was an easy walk to the TourEiffel, Invalides, and much more. Don't miss the Rue Cler early in the morning as the shop keepers clean the sidewalks and set up for the day. We used the Yellow Van Shuttle (booked throught the hotel) which was a good value and punctual. Buy the museum multi-day pass, and if you are a walker skip the Metro carne or passport. In 4 days we used the RER once to Versailles and the metro once to Montmarte. Special thank you to Frederika for her warm welcome and helpful suggestions.

<Author>SanRamonTraveler
<Content>Loved the Hotel Relais Bosquet We just returned from a 7 day/6 night stay at this hotel and it was wonderful. The staff is extremely friendly and helpful. They provided us with some great restaurant/cafe recommendations and helped us figure out which metro trains to take to get to major sites. On our last night there, the night clerk even gave us a ride to the Latin Quarter and showed us around! The room was comfortable (we had a standard twin) with a nice bathroom (tub/shower) and we even had a partial view of the Eiffel Tower out of our window (all that for 105 Euro's). Best of all though, is the location of this hotel in the Rue Cler neighborhood. If you want to stay in a residential neighborhood with a 10 minute walk to the Eiffel Tower and a 25-30 minute walk to the Orsay and Rodin museums, a cheese shop, small supermarket, numerous patisseries, wine shops, deli's, cafes, and boutiques around the corner then this is the place for you!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Incredible city, wonderful hotel... My wife and I had the pleasure of spending 4 nights here in July 2004, and couldn't have been happier. It was my first visit to Paris, and the location in the Rue Cler neighborhood was superb. Quaint shops, great cafes and bistros EVERYWHERE you turn, and only a couple blocks from the Metro. We even had a view of the Eiffel Tower! Our room was very clean and comfortable, the bathrooms were modern and spotless, and the air conditioning was a lifesaver in the summertime. Also, the elevator, roughly the size of a telephone booth, is both fun and a real welcome to Europe. We laughed for hours! For only 105 euro, it's hard to beat The Relais Bosquet. The staff was helpful and friendly, as were all the Parisians we spoke with. Can't wait to go back, and will definately recommend this hotel to others.

<Content>Great Hotel This hotel has a fabulous location, a short walk to the Eiffel Tour, Napolean's Tomb, Rodin and D'Orsay Museums. The Metro stop is 1.5 blocks away, post office 2 blocks away, and the wonderful street market Rue Cler is just at the end of the block. Several bakeries and Cafe's are within a 2 block radius. The desk staff were very helpful and courteous at check-in and check-out, and also offered help with directions and the many other tourist questions we asked. The desk staff booked our city tour for us as well. The room was clean and comfortable with air-conditioning, mini-bar and electric black-out blinds. This Hotel was an excellent value in Paris, we would stay there again in a minute!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful experience The Relais Bosquet is a great Parisian hotel. The manager, Gerard, is courteous and very helpful. We had a fifth floor room with a view of the Eiffel Tower that was absolutely breathtaking at night. The rooms are spacious, clean and well appointed. We purchased pasteries at the corner bakery and ate breakfast in our room with the complementary coffee and tea. The location is extremely convenient with the Rue Cler just a block away, the Eifell tower about a ten minute walk, sidewalk cafes all around, and the Metro one block away. We walked to Napolean's Tomb, the Rodin, the Louvre and the Orsay Museums. We will definitely stay there again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The most wonderful Parisian hotel My sister  I spent two glorious weeks at the Relais Bosquet in April this year and LOVED every minute of it. This was certainly not our first trip to France. However, this time we decided to rent an apartment. Big, gigantic mistake using the agency we chose. Wrong area, seedy, smelly apartment and the cost for that mistake was one full night rent just to break the lease. The big plus was finding Relais Bosquet and the sweet, friendly, helpful people. We will not stay anywhere else in Paris after finding them. It is bright, squeaky clean, decorated in beautiful colors, a refrigerator and two safes. shower  tub, fantastic electric blinds, excellent lighting, and the rooms are large and spacious with more than adequate storage. I noticed most of the reviews were for shorter stays than ours but within that two weeks time, we found nothing that disappointed us concerning the Hotel. It is convenient to dry cleaners, Caf茅 de Marche (yummm) a neighborhood bistro with excellent food and terrific service; a grocer that also carries the wonderful French coffee, Caf茅 Noir; bakeries, pastry shops, chocolates, fantastic chocolates, flower shops, a post office just around the corner, a perfect shop to purchase very economical luggage to bring all the French treasures home one did not plan on - like $29 for a very large duffle with zippers  pockets  locks, oh, and at that same shop, large Paris bags with various designs  Eifffel Tower keychains attached sold much cheaper than we found elsewhere, bus stop nearly at the door, two Metro stops very close by, ATM nearby. Can't say enough good things about the owner and his staff. They tolerated our poor French with their excellent English, went far beyond what most concierges would go to help us. There is not one of those people I would not truly want to invite into my home, including the housekeeping staff. This group of people are exceptional which may account for the exceptional beauty of the Hotel. Stay here one time and you've found your home away from home in Paris.   
<Date>Jun 25, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Relais Bosquet My husband and I stayed at the hotel Sept. 2003 and loved the hotel, staff and general area. We became hysterical when the elevator door opened because it was SO small!! Our room was a nice surprise, bright,clean and perfect size. Quiet, too. A coffee maker in the room was great to have in the am. Only had breakfast there once because there are so many cafes and bakeries around. Metro and Eiffel Tower are within 5-10 min. walking distance. Took metro to Monmarte, loved the area. Ate at several local cafes and restaurants, our favorites were La Florimund a short walk away and La Polidor in the 6th arrondiss. not far from Luxembourg Gdns. People were friendly and appreciated our lame attempts at French. Take the Seine pm cruise, use the Batobus on the Seine to get around and buy treats on Rue Cler and at Flo Prestige, a gourmet take-out store. Will go back to Paris next spring but may try an apartment, if not, we will definitely stay here again.
